### Post by EMCGFX on 2010-04-27
Hi guys, I thought its about time to create a post for people like me that cant wait to see version 10.04 final :lolflag: Its two more days :guitar: Grabbing :popcorn: and waiting it out in here :P Any one interested in joining me here hahahhahaha Yeah I've became real Ubuntu fan what can I say.

[IMG]http://countdown.immanuel-peratoner.de/[/IMG]

My Ubuntu System Specs:
-- Intel(R) Core(TM)2 Quad CPU Q6600 @ 2.40GHz
-- 4GB DDR2 Memory & 250GB Hard Drive
-- GeForce 9400 GT, PCI-E 16x, 1024 MB, 550 MHz
-- ViewSonic VX2025wm 20.1" LCD + DELL E173FP 17" LCD

Some Ubuntu 10.04 RC issues that I've noticed. I used upgrade not clean install, so that may be why I get this issues. In any case I hope this all will be fixed in final release.

#1. When I use TwinView with two LCDs and watching dvd in VLC, when video moves from side to side I see my VLC picture cut most of the time. I haven't found any solution for this yet. I used to be able to use Xinerama in version 9.10 final and this eliminated this issue. But I could not use any of compiz effects. I prefer to use TwinView instead, this way I have all effects. This is not that big of a deal. But it should work better. Now using one display works perfectly fine, its that when I use this two LCD that when I get this issue. I don't know if its because I'm using two different LCD displays or if its video card drivers problem.

#2. Sometimes upon boot I get my WD 640GB HDD not mounted for some reason. I need to reboot again for it to work. This is the newer model of WD HDD. I have no idea what is up with that. It works perfectly fine.

#3. Applying wallpaper for two LCDs, I used to be able to stretch wallpaper between two LCDs. Now I see same wallpaper on two LCDs. Stretch don't work properly.  Span works but that not what I need.

#4. Keep Align Icons not saving upon reboot.

will update this post ones I found more issues ;)

### Post by mockingbird on 2010-04-28
The reason why your video is cutting:

This problem occures when the video plays at a higher framerate than the monitor's refresh rate.  This is called vertical sync.

This problem is known with VLC, and I hope in the future they include an option to ENABLE vertical sync when playing videos.

### Post by mihai.ile on 2010-04-28
daily build means the current version of the day (today), the rc is actualy the daily build on dayX such as final release which would be the last daily build.

Every day we get a daily build. it' like a version release every day for testing,etc.

### Post by recluce on 2010-04-28
I have been testing Lucid Lynx since Alpha 1. After an initial Oopla with the Alpha 1 installation I reinstalled from the Alpha 2 image and have just updated since. The system is rock stable, even more so than Jaunty (Karmic was a dud for my system). So will I reinstall from the final release image? NO. No reaon to, just a waste of time. 

Very surprising: no rush of updates during the final hours before release, actually, there has been not a single update in 24 hours (using the main server).

Bottom line: if you have an up-to-date version of Lucid from the development branch, there is little incentive to do a fresh install of the final - unless you messed up your installation big time. :P

For everybody else: if you waited that long, you can wait another day! :lolflag:

### Post by 23meg on 2010-04-28
Wait for the official release announcement that will be posted to the [ubuntu-announce mailing list]("https://lists.ubuntu.com/mailman/listinfo/ubuntu-announce"). If you're not subscribed, you can check the web archive for April [here]("https://lists.ubuntu.com/archives/ubuntu-announce/2010-April/date.html").

No announcement, no release. Regardless of whether people post links that appear to be working, whether some random blog says "it's released", or even whether the Ubuntu home page is updated to reflect the release.

Images can be updated at any point before release, and mirrors need to sync up. By downloading before the release announcement, you risk getting a broken half-updated image, and slowing the syncing of the mirrors (which will potentially delay the release).

---

### Post by 23meg on 2010-04-28
> **lesliefrancis said:**
> <snip>

What about the above link which claims to have the final release of 10.4?

It doesn't claim to have the final release. Did you read the index.html file there? Let me paste it here:

>  Images are distributed here so that mirrors can pick them up in time before release. Images here may not be final even if they look as if they are; by distributing pre-release images here we can make final mirroring faster.

Please do not attempt to download images directly from this directory; by doing so, you are likely to contribute to delaying the release for everyone else, since we will have to wait longer for worldwide mirroring to complete.

-- Ubuntu Release Team

### Post by 23meg on 2010-04-29
> **msmooth said:**
> Just finished backup all my files. its 12:05 am... any idea of what hour they release the final iso? not in a hurry just curious. thanks

> **ToxicBurn said:**
> so when do you think they will post the final iso. soon or late in the day on the 29th

It's impossible to tell when precisely it's going to happen. [The release is a laborious process]("https://wiki.ubuntu.com/ReleaseProcess"), performed by **multiple people working in different timezones**, and its completion depends, among other things, on when mirrors complete syncing, which in turn depends on network conditions all over the world.

### Post by Merk42 on 2010-04-29
> **Mike BFD said:**
> Seems like everybody's waiting for the release to download ISO and make a "clean install"... I just wander if I'll be able to upgrade to final version - or it's a stupid question?

If you're running 8.04 or 9.10 you'll be able to upgrade through the usual upgrade manager. It'll say new distribution available.

If you're running Lucid Lynx Alpha/Beta/RC there will be no prompt about a new distribution, but any upgrades will give you the final version.

### Post by Baldrick_NZ on 2010-04-29
> **Merk42 said:**
> I think Canonical deliberately doesn't mention an exact time because their servers get hit hard enough on the day as it is. Could you imagine how bad it would be if everyone hit the same minute?

Which is why I reckon Canonical would be extremely wise to do what most software vendors do...

Schedule the release gradually from timezone to timezone.

IE: Midnight 29th (Wed night - Thur Morn) Release to UTC +12, an hour later, UTC +11; an hour later, UTC +10, etc...

That way the release is staggered meaning everyone gets it at the same time in their own timezones. This would also ease congestion on the servers. Not everyone who wants it when it finally is released will be trying at exactly the same time!

How would that work? Any ideas?

Ofcourse, as an added bonus, we in NZ would be the first to benefit. ;-)

---

### Post by Merk42 on 2010-04-29

Ofcourse, as an added bonus, we in NZ would be the first to benefit. ;-)

It wouldn't work, because then people here in the US would just download from the NZ servers...

### Post by Niksko on 2010-04-29
> **slither1109 said:**
> I removed the link, after looking closer it seems that it is not from the official chinese ubuntu website. Im not gonna take my chances, I canceled the download and am waiting for an official one. So impatient!

Well, it's just that if you go to [http://ubuntu.srt.cn/ubuntu-releases/.pool/](http://ubuntu.srt.cn/ubuntu-releases/.pool/) you get a message that says:
" Images are distributed here so that mirrors can pick them up in time before release. Images here may not be final even if they look as if they are; by distributing pre-release images here we can make final mirroring faster.

Please do not attempt to download images directly from this directory; by doing so, you are likely to contribute to delaying the release for everyone else, since we will have to wait longer for worldwide mirroring to complete.

-- Ubuntu Release Team "

Also, the page title is "This is not the page you are looking for; move along". Hehehhe

### Post by buellman on 2010-04-29
For those of you planing to refresh until release: get some more coffee/popcorn/ ... could take a few hours from now on :-) Why?

If you look [here]("https://lists.ubuntu.com/archives/ubuntu-announce/") and search for the release announcements you will find that they are pretty much the same on every release:

Ubuntu 9.10 released
Ubuntu Announcements
Thu Oct 29 14:25:46 GMT 2009

Ubuntu 9.04 released
Ubuntu Announcements
Thu Apr 23 13:53:26 BST 2009

Ubuntu 8.10 released
Ubuntu Announcements
Thu Oct 30 14:11:31 GMT 2008

Ubuntu 8.04 LTS released
Ubuntu Announcements
Thu Apr 24 13:17:20 BST 2008

Ubuntu 7.10 released
Ubuntu Announcements
Thu Oct 18 12:15:03 BST 2007

Ubuntu 7.04 released
Ubuntu Announcements
Thu Apr 19 15:18:16 BST 2007

So... wild guess: 10.04 will be **official** released at 14:00:00 GMT +/- 1 or 2 hours :-)

Greets. Buellman

Hmmm... yes, possibly. But then, that would be somewhat misleading considering it would be a day late in some parts of the world. 3pm UTC would technically mean both Eastern Australia and NZ wouldn't get to see it on the 29th, as advertised, but instead a day late (on the 30th).

### Post by neglesaks on 2010-04-29
> **thunderbox said:**
> Just use the update manager. it should ahve the option to upgrade. if it does not you have to make it look for a new version. im not 100% on how to do that. so im not going to give advice

The update manager fetches updates off the repositories, and immediately following release and a number of days after that, they will be swamped with people downloading off it.

If you want to update your system with least hassle, use the Update Manager, but wait a few days.

Else, help everyone and download the final ISO's via bittorrent. It's also enomuously faster.

the only time i ever tried rpms was way back when i was first looking into linux. I heard about redhat being the goto for desktop linux versions. And well it didn't feel that natural for me.

Then i saw ubuntu and started on it and it just well worked and was nice. Although i had to compile my own wireless driver for my old laptop it was still a nice and good experience. Ubuntu just worked and debian is really nice and feels cool and natural. 

RPM based OSes to me seem to be more geared to the person who's not so much about useability but a tad bit more perfromance at a cost for it. Debian based systems seem to try to go for usability at the cost of some performance ie they're not the more efficient distro on the market but they just work which is what every computer user wants at the end of the day.

Those links are for mirroring, have a look at [http://ubuntu.media.mit.edu/ubuntu-releases/.pool/:](http://ubuntu.media.mit.edu/ubuntu-releases/.pool/:)


> 
 Images are distributed here so that mirrors can pick them up in time before release. Images here may not be final even if they look as if they are; by distributing pre-release images here we can make final mirroring faster.

Please do not attempt to download images directly from this directory; by doing so, you are likely to contribute to delaying the release for everyone else, since we will have to wait longer for worldwide mirroring to complete.

-- Ubuntu Release Team

### Post by dudumomo on 2010-04-29
As you may know, there is an important bug with this release.
[https://bugs.launchpad.net/ubuntu/+source/ubiquity/+bug/570765](https://bugs.launchpad.net/ubuntu/+source/ubiquity/+bug/570765)

> We've decided to respin the 32bit and 64bit CDs of Ubuntu Desktop *ONLY*, as we feel this gives us the widest spread fix possible and allows us to still release today (April 29th). Unfortunately, this means other affected variants, such as Xubuntu, will not have this fix, and we deeply apologize for this.

### Post by 23meg on 2010-04-29
> **Arthur_D said:**
> I'm just refreshing here because I know all you ubuntu.com refreshers will post it here the minute it's ready - so no need for me to do the same as you. :P

And they will all be [missing the point]("http://ubuntuforums.org/showpost.php?p=9189391&postcount=72"), and unnecessarily stressing the servers.

If I were you, I'd either subscribe to the very low-traffic [ubuntu-announce mailing list]("https://lists.ubuntu.com/mailman/listinfo/ubuntu-announce") to get notified by mail when the release happens, or refresh [this page]("https://lists.ubuntu.com/archives/ubuntu-announce/2010-April/date.html"), since the only true indicator that the release is out is the announcement mail sent to the list by the release manager. Yes, that means that the home page may be updated a while before or after the actual release, and that's normal.

### Post by 23meg on 2010-04-29
> **sweetafton said:**
> How long does a respin take?

A respin of the whole set of images takes nearly two days, which has two potentially important implications: 

[list] [*] Developers who are in London for the release sprint will be flying home and/or be completely exhausted at the time the release happens, and may be unable to respond to any possible incidents unfolding right after release 


[*] Since the respin would be completed on May 1st, the release would technically be Ubuntu 10.05, not .04, which doesn't look pretty.[/list]
Every effort is being made to complete the release as soon as possible, and that *may* involve the small compromise of some images not receiving the fix. 

In any case, the fix will be immediately available as an update upon installation.

---

### Post by Zealhybrid on 2010-04-29

### Post by andrewabc on 2010-04-29
> **arophous said:**
> Reminds me, I need to go buy some blank disks...

:popcorn:

Make sure to use cd-rw

As to how to install via liveusb.
system->administration->USB startup Disk Creator

liveusb is much faster if you are testing it. Installing from liveusb can sometimes make your cd-rom not work due to it thinking usb is cd-rom. Something to fix in fstab. Not sure if it has been fixed for 10.04 or not. You can try it and if cd-rom not auto recognized from install you can always install from cd-rom.

---

### Post by naja on 2010-04-29

[http://unetbootin.sourceforge.net/](http://unetbootin.sourceforge.net/)
choose iso or let it download the distro for you and let it copy data to usb when done reboot from usb.

### Post by andrewabc on 2010-04-29
> **mo79 said:**
> I have a Toshiba NB100 that I bought 2yrs ago that came with 8.04, so will I still be able to upgrade to 10.04 through the update manager? 
It has never informed me about subsequent (albeit non LTS) releases to date, is that normal?

It should have notified you of 8.10.

And it should notify you of 10.04
Yes it's possible to upgrade from 8.04 to 10.04.
Although you might be better off backing up data and format/install for best results. Although first I'd try running liveusb to make sure it works with your hardware. No point in upgrading if there are stuff/hardware that doesn't work.

---

### Post by thenailedone on 2010-04-29

---

### Post by Merk42 on 2010-04-29
> **mo79 said:**
> I have a Toshiba NB100 that I bought 2yrs ago that came with 8.04, so will I still be able to upgrade to 10.04 through the update manager? 
It has never informed me about subsequent (albeit non LTS) releases to date, is that normal?

If your provider set it to only inform you of LTS it's perfectly normal.  You can check under System > Administration > Software Sources > Updates
Under "Release Upgrade" it's probably set to "Long term support releases only"

So at some point today the update manager will do its usual thing except it'll say "New distribution available 10.04", then it'll go about updating.

---

### Post by Jon Monreal on 2010-04-29
> **mo79 said:**
> I have a Toshiba NB100 that I bought 2yrs ago that came with 8.04, so will I still be able to upgrade to 10.04 through the update manager? 
It has never informed me about subsequent (albeit non LTS) releases to date, is that normal?

You should be able to upgrade from LTS to LTS.

Update Manager should inform you of every release. It is likely set to LTS only. To fix this, go to Software Sources and switch to the Updates tab. Below there will be a section called "Release upgrade". Change that from "Long term support releases only" to "Normal releases".

### Post by Cheesemill on 2010-04-29
> **mihai007 said:**
> do you have specific commands that will work for the release?

First install zsync:
```
aptitude -y install zsync
```

Then just change into the directory where you've downloaded the daily build and type:
```
zsync -i <name-of-daily-iso-file> http://url-of-final-release.iso.zsync
```

You will find the link for the zsync file on the download page [here]("http://cdimage.ubuntu.com/releases/lucid/") when it is released.

---

### Post by chariotoffire on 2010-04-29
Not sure if this has been posted before, but this code will automatically download the new release when it comes out.

```
while true; do if wget http://releases.ubuntu.com/10.04/ubuntu-10.04-desktop-i386.iso.torrent; then ktorrent --silent ubuntu-10.04-desktop-i386.iso.torrent ; date; break; else sleep 60; fi; done

```I tested it with the 9.10 release, so I'm assuming it will work for 10.04. You may need to change the torrent command depending on the client you're using.

If you have fast internet, just get the cd.

DVD just has more packages which means if you were to install a piece of software it can get it from DVD instead of internet. Which is usually helpful for people on dialup or no internet connection.

### Post by andrewabc on 2010-04-29
> **lazymangaka said:**
> I'm a bit confused. If I'm running the RC on a system upgraded from Karmic, and everything is running perfectly for me, is there any advantage to downloading a fresh version? Wouldn't I just lose everything I've done so far? Or, if everything is running fine right now, would it just be best to wait for the updates to roll in and get the final version that way?

Yes keep using what you are using. It will turn into the final.

Since you upgraded from karmic, I'd suggest that in a day or so download 10.04 final and put on one of your cd or liveusb in case you ever need to format/install it.

There are some minor advantages to having fresh format/install of 10.04 over 9.10 upgraded. If your 10.04 upgrade seems to be running fine, then keep using it. Otherwise feel free to format/install 10.04

### Post by gmc on 2010-04-29
I just saw this cool script at [http://www.commandlinefu.com](http://www.commandlinefu.com)

> 
while true; do if wget [http://releases.ubuntu.com/10.04/ubuntu-10.04-desktop-i386.iso.torrent;](http://releases.ubuntu.com/10.04/ubuntu-10.04-desktop-i386.iso.torrent;) then ktorrent --silent ubuntu-10.04-desktop-i386.iso.torrent ; date; break; else sleep 60; fi; done
It'll loop until the official iso arrives and then start ktorrent (replace with your favorite client) and download it.

I thought it was petty cool. Thanks to user [ppaschka]("http://www.commandlinefu.com/commands/by/ppaschka") at commandlinefu.

G

### Post by darkhero on 2010-04-29
> **ubfu said:**
> How you modified the notifier ? nice theme you got there , is it default 10.04 theme ?

please follow this link: [http://manpages.ubuntu.com/manpages/gutsy/man1/notify-send.1.html](http://manpages.ubuntu.com/manpages/gutsy/man1/notify-send.1.html)

or you could just type it directly in the terminal, the command is **[FONT=Courier New][SIZE=2]notify-send[/SIZE][/FONT]** if it's not installed yet, bash will suggest the correct package to install, just follow it. then [SIZE=2]**[FONT=Courier New]man notify-send[/FONT]**[/SIZE] for more info.

about the theme, i think i got it last year from [http://gnome-look.org]("http://gnome-look.org/")

### Post by andrewabc on 2010-04-29
> **Saorex said:**
> Question for you guys... I remember reading somewhere that the AMD64 image is "only" for AMD64 processors. People with let's say Intel Core2, i5 or i7 processors should get another build (can't remember the exact name).

### Post by nderic77 on 2010-04-29
> **priegog said:**
> I'm intrigued... how can torrents work but not normal downloads?

Normal downloads still work, but the latency to India means that they can take a lot longer. Torrents download from multiple (hundreds, if not thousands) of hosts and thus are optimized for lower latency.

### Post by markrocha on 2010-04-29
> **priegog said:**
> I'm intrigued... how can torrents work but not normal downloads?
 
downloads work too. it's just that in india, our internet connections are really slow, so a single download of 750 mb will take too long. that's why we prefer torrents, on a half mb line, it should take around 4 to 6 hours (torrent) as opposed to a single d'load which will take 12 to 14 hours!

---

### Post by randomizer101 on 2010-04-29
> **priegog said:**
> I'm intrigued... how can torrents work but not normal downloads?

Because it's faster to download from multiple overseas (or better yet, local) connections than a single overseas connection that is being slaughtered by other users. Torrents are much faster for me as well unless I find a decent local mirror, but even then speeds vary.

---

### Post by yellerKat on 2010-04-29
> **nderic77 said:**
> Normal downloads still work, but the latency to India means that they can take a lot longer. Torrents download from multiple (hundreds, if not thousands) of hosts and thus are optimized for lower latency.

Thanks, that makes sense!

### Post by andrewabc on 2010-04-29
> **oleink said:**
> How do you use the torrents to upgrade.  Cant you just use the update manager???????? (this is my first time upgrading I've only used 9.10)

You can't really use torrents to upgrade from 9.10->10.04. Well you could but it's easier to just wait for update manager to tell you 10.04 has been released and follow isntructions.

The main reason to download using torrents is so the servers don't die. You end up with same .iso image as regular download.

A man was stopped at a checkpoint on the way home from a visit to  Mexico. The blond border guard said, "Get out of the car and open the  trunk!" 

The traveler replied, "I'm sorry, but the handbrake on the car is  broken. I can't take my foot off the brake or it'll roll backwards!" 

The guard, "Do you take me for a FOOL?! That won't keep me from  inspecting things!" 

He gets into the car himself, in the passenger's seat, and applies the  brake himself. 

"Now," he says, "That takes care of that, now go and open the trunk!!" 

So the traveler complies and opens the trunk of the car. 

"Now", shouts the guard from inside the car, "Are  there any drugs or contraband in there?

### Post by magicdave26 on 2010-04-29
**Desktop CD**

  The desktop CD allows you to try Ubuntu without changing your computer at all, and at your option to install it permanently later. This type of CD is what most people will want to use. You will need at least 256MB of RAM to install from this CD.
  There are two images available, each for a different type of  computer:
  [PC  (Intel x86) desktop CD]("http://releases.ubuntu.com/10.04/ubuntu-10.04-desktop-i386.iso")  For almost all PCs. This includes most machines with  Intel/AMD/etc type processors and almost all computers that run Microsoft Windows, as well  as newer Apple Macintosh systems based on Intel processors. Choose this if  you are at all unsure.[64-bit  PC (AMD64) desktop CD]("http://releases.ubuntu.com/10.04/ubuntu-10.04-desktop-amd64.iso")  Choose this to take full advantage of computers based on the  AMD64 or EM64T architecture (e.g., Athlon64, Opteron, EM64T Xeon, Core 2). If you have a non-64-bit processor made by AMD, or if you need full support for 32-bit code, use the Intel x86 images instead.

---

### Post by dilodicus on 2010-04-29
I'm getting what appears to be the final release on the releases page, the iso names are different, if you are still getting RC isos then copy the link address and just remove "-rc" from the name

eg

[http://releases.ubuntu.com/10.04/ubuntu-10.04-rc-desktop-i386.iso](http://releases.ubuntu.com/10.04/ubuntu-10.04-rc-desktop-i386.iso)

becomes

[http://releases.ubuntu.com/10.04/ubuntu-10.04-desktop-i386.iso](http://releases.ubuntu.com/10.04/ubuntu-10.04-desktop-i386.iso)

I'm going to start backing up for a fresh install :)
